**What landed:**

1. **`src/ui/Theme.h` extended** (+79 LOC). New types: `Mode { Dark, Light }`, `Preset { Noir, Midnight, Ember, Forest, Lavender, Arctic, Warm }`, `ThemePalette` struct (16 color slots), `ThemePresetEntry` struct, `kPresets` constexpr array of 7 entries with the exact bg0/bg1/accent/accentRgb values from audit § 1.2. API decls: `resolvePalette(mode, preset)`, `buildStylesheet(palette)`, `applyTheme(app, mode, preset)`, `applyThemeFromSettings(app)`, `current()`, `loadMode/loadPreset/saveMode/savePreset`, `slugFor`/`*FromSlug`. Existing scaffolding (kBg, kPanel, kAccent, etc. + sizing tokens) kept verbatim — TileCard.cpp's `Theme::kAccent` callsite stays valid. Renamed `enum class Mode { Comics, Books, ... } → AppSection` to free the `Mode` name for the new Dark/Light enum; old enum had no callers per audit history.

2. **`src/ui/Theme.cpp` NEW** (624 LOC). Holds `darkBaselineNoir()` palette factory (byte-equal to today's noirStylesheet literals + applyDarkPalette QPalette mapping), the full ~377-line QSS template as a `QStringLiteral` with 16 `__PLACEHOLDER__` tokens, `buildStylesheet(palette)` doing the substitution loop via `QHash` + `.replace()`, `buildQPalette(palette)` for the QPalette mapping (Highlight uses `QColor(palette.accent)` at alpha 0x38 matching today's behavior), `applyTheme()` composing setPalette + setStyleSheet + updating the `current()` cache, `applyThemeFromSettings()` reading two separate keys (`theme/mode` + `theme/preset`) via `QSettings("Tankoban", "Tankoban")` matching the codebase convention, slug ↔ enum round-trip helpers.

3. **`src/main.cpp` simplified** (-390 LOC net). Deleted `applyDarkPalette()` + `noirStylesheet()` definitions (rolled into Theme.cpp). Boot now calls `Theme::applyThemeFromSettings(app)` instead of the two-line palette+stylesheet pair. Added `#include "ui/Theme.h"`.

4. **`CMakeLists.txt`** — added `src/ui/Theme.cpp` to the source list next to `src/ui/MainWindow.cpp` (1 line).

**Substitution table (16 placeholders).** `__BG__`, `__BG1__`, `__TEXT__`, `__TEXT_DIM__`, `__MUTED__`, `__BORDER__`, `__BORDER_HI__`, `__ACCENT__`, `__ACCENT_SOFT__`, `__ACCENT_LINE__`, `__TOPBAR_BG__`, `__SIDEBAR_BG__`, `__MENU_BG__`, `__TOAST_BG__`, `__CARD_BG__`, `__OVERLAY_DIM__`. For Dark+Noir, every placeholder resolves to the literal it replaced — the rendered stylesheet should be byte-identical to today's. Surface alphas (0.05/0.06/0.10/0.12/0.16/18/30/0.78/etc.) NOT placeholdered — they're transparency conventions, not theme-bound colors.

**Architecture decisions (Rule 14, mine):**
- Theme.cpp split out of main.cpp for clean ownership + future modification (P3 light-mode override, P4 Mica). main.cpp goes from ~530 LOC to 150 LOC.
- 16-token substitution loop runs once at boot; <1ms cost, negligible.
- QSettings split keys (`theme/mode` + `theme/preset`) — fixes Tankoban-Max's localStorage-shared-key boot-reset bug from audit § 1.4. Two SEPARATE `QSettings::value()` calls; each axis persists independently.
- `Theme::kAccent` constexpr stays at `"#c7a76b"` (Noir gold) for back-compat with TileCard's hover/select border. Future tile-color-follows-active-preset refactor lands in P2 or later if Hemanth wants it.
- One literal NOT placeholdered: `rgba(199,167,107,0.45)` at QLineEdit:focus border. One-off alpha (0.45 vs accentLine's 0.40); for non-Noir presets the focus border stays gold which is a known minor inconsistency. Acceptable for P1; P2/P3 cleanup possible.

**Fix 2 — chip-uncheck on popover dismiss.** Hemanth verbatim "I just clicked both audio and subtitle tracks. I opened them. now they have darkened shade for the rest of the time video is playing. ensure clicking icons do not darken them indefinitely." Root cause: chip `:checked` state is set true at the chip-click handler when the popover opens, but popover-internal dismiss paths (item click → onChoiceClicked → dismiss; click outside → eventFilter → dismiss; ESC) all called `dismiss()` → `hide()` and never propagated back to the chip. dismissOtherPopovers (sibling-chip-click path at VideoPlayer.cpp:507-518) already manually unchecked chips so it was fine, but the other paths left chips stuck-checked. Visible "darkened shade" = the `:checked` gradient at VideoPlayer.cpp:1384-1389.

**Shape (a) per brief — popover-emits-signal:**
- Added `void dismissed();` signal to SubtitlePopover.h + AudioPopover.h + SettingsPopover.h (one-line add per .h, alongside existing `hoverChanged(bool)`).
- Emitted from the single chokepoint `dismiss()` body in each .cpp (alongside the existing `hoverChanged(false)` emit from the prior wake's HUD-lifecycle fix). dismiss() is the chokepoint for ALL popover-internal close paths.
- Connected in VideoPlayer.cpp around the existing hoverChanged connects (lines ~1863-1898) to drive `chip->setChecked(false)`. Three new 3-line connect blocks per popover.

**Code-walk coverage of all dismiss paths (the verification-before-completion proof):**
1. **Item-click** (user picks a sub/audio track or +/- button on Settings) → onChoiceClicked / onItemClicked / +/- handler → calls `dismiss()` → emit dismissed → chip uncheck ✓
2. **Click-outside** (user clicks anywhere outside popover bounds) → eventFilter catches QEvent::MouseButtonPress + position outside → calls `dismiss()` → emit ✓
3. **Chip-click-while-open** (user toggles chip with popover already open) → toggle() detects isVisible() true → calls `dismiss()` → emit dismissed → chip uncheck. Then toggle() returns; the click handler at VideoPlayer.cpp:1605/1620/1636 follows up with `chip->setChecked(m_popover->isOpen())` which evaluates to `setChecked(false)` (popover just hidden) — harmless redundant set ✓
4. **dismissOtherPopovers** (user clicks a sibling chip) → calls `popover->hide()` directly, NOT dismiss(), so signal does NOT fire — BUT this code path already manually unchecks the sibling chip via the existing `if (m_<X>Chip) m_<X>Chip->setChecked(false)` line at VideoPlayer.cpp:509/513/517. Coverage complete via the manual line ✓

All three popovers covered (SubtitlePopover + AudioPopover + SettingsPopover). Net diff: +18 LOC across 3 .h + 3 .cpp + +9 LOC across VideoPlayer.cpp.

**Hemanth verbatim:** "the time (current playing time / full length of the video) is not loading immediately after opening a video."

**Root cause:** `m_timeLabel` + `m_durLabel` only updated in `onTimeUpdate` at VideoPlayer.cpp:1083 + 1101-1108, which fires post-first-frame at ~1Hz. Between openFile reset to "—:—" at :593-594 and the first time_update event, labels lagged by seconds-to-minutes on slow opens. Phase 1.1 already decoupled metadata via `media_info` post-probe emission for title + loading-overlay + HDR + chapters + audio_device — duration was the missing field. Same `feedback_sidecar_metadata_decoupling.md` rule applied to time labels.

**Sidecar audit:** `media_info` JSON at native_sidecar/src/main.cpp:449-462 carries hdr / color_primaries / color_trc / max_cll / max_fall / chapters / audio_device / audio_host_api but NOT duration. duration_ms IS in `probe_done` payload (main.cpp:335) but SidecarProcess::probeDone signal only forwards the duration_is_estimate bool.

**Fix shape (a) per brief — duration via media_info:**

- **native_sidecar/src/main.cpp** — added `mi["duration_sec"] = probe->duration_sec;` after `mi["audio_host_api"]` and before `write_event("media_info", ...)`. probe->duration_sec already populated at this point in open_worker — no new probe code, just exposing existing data.

- **VideoPlayer.cpp mediaInfo lambda** (line 1961+) — added new block right after `m_isHdr` capture: extracts `duration_sec`, populates `m_durationSec` + `m_durLabel` (with `~` prefix when m_durationIsEstimate true, mirrors onTimeUpdate :1101-1108) + `m_seekBar->setDurationSec` + optimistic `m_timeLabel = "0:00"`. duration <= 0 leaves labels at teardownUi's "—:—" (no lying when probe couldn't extract usable duration).

**Code-walk verification:**
1. Sidecar payload includes duration_sec — main.cpp:462 area.
2. mediaInfo signal flows JSON unchanged — SidecarProcess.cpp:576 emit.
3. mediaInfo fires post-probe — emission order: probe_done (main.cpp:331) → media_info (:462). m_durationIsEstimate cached at :1797-1810 BEFORE mediaInfo lambda runs.
4. teardownUi reset preserved — :593-594 unchanged.
5. Stream-mode stall gate doesn't apply — :1067 gateHud is mid-playback only.
6. No regression to onTimeUpdate — body untouched; new mediaInfo population just runs earlier.

With equal min-width + equal stretch on the side wraps, centerWrap's geometry midpoint = toolbar midpoint regardless of how many right-cluster buttons are visible (multi-volume case has 6 buttons / 286px content; single-volume has 3 buttons / 148px — both fit under the 320 min-width floor so center stays centered either way). Old single-flat-tbLayout addStretch() pattern produced visible left-of-center page-block because the side cluster widths were asymmetric (back btn 40px vs right cluster 320px) — equal-stretch can't compensate. **(2) Page label drops "Page" prefix** — all three setText sites updated (initial constructor :588 "Page 1 / 1" → "1 / 1"; updatePageLabel single-page :1531 "Page %1 / %2" → "%1 / %2"; updatePageLabel double-page :1526 "Pages %1-%2 / %3" → "%1-%2 / %3"). The 1px white-alpha-0.10 border-top separator kept (it provides visual detachment without competing with the "all solid black" feel). READY TO COMMIT - [Agent 4, STREAM_PLAYER_LIFECYCLE_FIXUPS — Bug 1 setFocus on stream playback start + Bug 2 stopPlayback before stopStream in close handler; both parity restorations with MainWindow::openVideoPlayer / closeVideoPlayer (MainWindow.cpp:545-557); build_check.bat BUILD OK first try; no MCP per Agent 4's visual-verify lane]: Hemanth verbatim 2-bug report on stream-mode lifecycle: "1. I can't pause the video in stream mode. 2. The video keeps playing even after I close the video." Both root-caused via direct comparison with MainWindow's video-library flow which has the matching calls; StreamPage's parallel flow was missing them. **Bug 1 — Pause non-functional (root cause CONFIRMED):** launchPlayer lambda in onReadyToPlay at StreamPage.cpp:2218-2227 calls `player->openFile(...); player->setGeometry(...); player->show(); player->raise();` but never `player->setFocus()`. Without explicit focus, keyboard input continues going to whichever widget had focus before the player opened (search input / tile / etc.) — Space (mapped to toggle_pause via KeyBindings.cpp:5) and every other shortcut never reach VideoPlayer::keyPressEvent at :3198. MainWindow's video-library flow at MainWindow.cpp:551 has the matching `m_videoPlayer->setFocus();` immediately after show+raise — ship that line. Cite-comment STREAM_PLAYER_FOCUS_FIX 2026-04-25 references both the Hemanth-reported behavior + the MainWindow precedent. **Bug 2 — Close doesn't stop playback (root cause CONFIRMED):** closeRequested handler at StreamPage.cpp:2105 calls `m_playerController->stopStream()` (which only removes the engine-side torrent via the stream-server REST `/:hash/remove`) but never `player->stopPlayback()`. The sidecar process keeps running with already-buffered HTTP bytes flowing through the audio decoder; audio + video continue playing until the buffer drains (multiple seconds on HD content). MainWindow's closeVideoPlayer at MainWindow.cpp:557 calls `m_videoPlayer->stopPlayback();` which fires sendStop + sendShutdown to the sidecar (per VideoPlayer.cpp:617-660), gracefully closing the AV pipeline. Added `player->stopPlayback();` BEFORE `m_playerController->stopStream();` — sidecar tears down its own pipeline first, then engine frees the torrent. Reverse order would yank the HTTP source from under an in-flight ffmpeg read and let an error propagate. Cite-comment STREAM_PLAYER_CLOSE_FIX 2026-04-25 references the Hemanth bug + MainWindow precedent. **Honest scope on Bug 2:** the lifecycle gap was actually present at STREAM_SERVER_PIVOT Phase 3 ship (00:16 today) — Phase 3's "zero orphan processes" claim was specifically app-shutdown destructor cleanup (StreamServerEngine::~D-tor calls stopStream + writes `stopped via=dtor` telemetry), NOT in-app close. Hemanth's prior Phase 3 + Phase 2A/2B smokes never exercised in-app close + observe-keep-playing; he caught it this wake. Phase 3 evidence stands but the user-facing close-path was always going to need this fix; doesn't invalidate Phase 3, but the wake summary was scoped narrower than I had implied. **Diagnosis path (per /superpowers:systematic-debugging):** read closeRequested handler at :2105 → confirmed only stopStream wired → read controller's stopStream at StreamPlayerController.cpp:90 → confirmed it only does engine-side cleanup → read pause flow togglePause:2141 → sendPause:171 → handle_pause sidecar path at native_sidecar/src/main.cpp:1004 → confirmed the IPC path is intact end-to-end → read MainWindow::openVideoPlayer + closeVideoPlayer → spotted `setFocus` + `stopPlayback` calls absent in StreamPage's parallel flow. Both root causes empirically anchored to file:line pairs; no fix-without-confirmed-RC violation. **Build:** `cmd.exe //C "build_check.bat"` BUILD OK first try. **No MCP** per Agent 4's standard visual-verify pattern (Hemanth opens build_and_run.bat → Stream tab → plays a stream → presses Space + Space + closes → verifies pause + clean stop). **Discipline:** /superpowers:systematic-debugging (evidence-first); /simplify (1-line parity restorations + cite-comments, zero abstraction); /security-review (UI-lifecycle only, no new input surface, no new IPC commands — sendStop+sendShutdown wires were already in place); /superpowers:requesting-code-review (diff trivial: launchPlayer +1 line + comment block, closeRequested lambda +1 line + comment block); /build-verify BUILD OK; /superpowers:verification-before-completion (claim shape "MainWindow does X, StreamPage didn't, now does" with X cited by file:line for both bugs; Hemanth smoke is the final empirical proof). **Expected smoke result:** Space mid-playback flips play/pause icon + audio freezes within ~50ms; Space again resumes; Esc/back/X-button close stops audio + video within ~50ms (was multiple seconds). The actual bug class is the close-button path's fire-and-forget `sendStop + sendShutdown` sequence at VideoPlayer.cpp:627-637 having NO wait + NO kill backstop after the IPC sends. **Mechanism**: when the sidecar's IPC dispatcher is busy (e.g., handle_set_tracks workers still draining via Agent 4's Phase A.1 fix at main.cpp:1415, or PortAudio mid-write to a buffered stream, or any other transient back-pressure), the queued `stop` and `shutdown` commands sit in the dispatcher queue — but the audio thread keeps running. Eventually the dispatcher unblocks and processes them, but the gap is the audible artifact. The `~SidecarProcess` destructor at SidecarProcess.cpp:88-100 ALREADY had a wait+kill pattern (`waitForFinished(3000); if still running, kill();`) but that destructor only runs on app exit — close-button just `hide()`s the player without destroying SidecarProcess. So pre-fix, audio kept playing across the entire close→reopen sequence until app exit. **The fix shape — three small edits**: (1) `src/ui/player/SidecarProcess.h:90+` — added `void ensureTerminated(int timeoutMs = 500);` public decl directly under sendShutdown with a 14-line comment block documenting the bug class + the timeout rationale. (2) `src/ui/player/SidecarProcess.cpp` — refactored destructor to call `ensureTerminated(3000)` (preserves prior 3-second app-exit budget); added the `ensureTerminated` implementation body — early-returns if already NotRunning (idempotent for double-calls in rapid close+open sequences); else `waitForFinished(timeoutMs)`; if still running, debugLog the timeout + pid + `m_process->kill()` + a brief 200ms reap so QProcess marks NotRunning before any immediately-following `start()` call inspects state. (3) `src/ui/player/VideoPlayer.cpp:617-637 (stopPlayback)` — added `m_sidecar->ensureTerminated(500);` immediately after the existing sendShutdown call, with a 9-line comment block explaining the bug + rationale for the 500ms timeout (covers typical ~50-100ms graceful-exit window with headroom; force-kill on timeout; synchronous GUI-thread block is acceptable on close-button path since latency budget tolerates half a second). **Why it works**: openFile at VideoPlayer.cpp:492 already calls `m_sidecar->start()` if not running, so terminating the process on close is safe — the next file open spawns a fresh sidecar (which the existing log already shows happens per-file: 5 sidecar starts in the most recent session). Pa_Terminate skip on force-kill is harmless (PortAudio runtime state lives in the process, dies with it; next Pa_Initialize fires fresh on next sidecar startup). **Builds**: `build_check.bat` BUILD OK first try; fresh `out/Tankoban.exe` at 01:14:12, newer than all three edited sources (SidecarProcess.h 01:12:46, SidecarProcess.cpp 01:12:58, VideoPlayer.cpp 01:13:15).
